the FAA.\n**(17)**\nNot fewer than 3 organizations representing certified collective bargaining representatives of airline pilots operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations.\n**(18)**\nAviation safety experts with specific knowledge of human factors or human factors experts with specific knowledge of aviation safety.\n**(19)**\nThe National Transportation Safety Board.\n**(20)**\nAny other representative the Administrator determines appropriate.\n##### (c) Considerations\nIn developing the final rule under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe safety benefits of collision prevention technologies;\n**(2)**\nrelevant regulations, guidance, and policies for traffic awareness and traffic advisory technology that uses ADS\u2013B In;\n**(3)**\nways in which ADS\u2013B In software applications can be used as of the date of enactment of this Act;\n**(4)**\nsoftware in existence on the date of enactment of this Act, and reasonably projected thereafter, that can predict aircraft movements, display surrounding traffic, and provide visual and audible traffic advisories;\n**(5)**\nthe margin of error and accuracy of software described in paragraph (4);\n**(6)**\nthe safety benefits of software described in paragraph (4) in preventing conflicts with both aircraft and ground vehicles on airport surfaces;\n**(7)**\nthe safety benefits of software described in paragraph (4) in informing pilots or flight crews of operational risks, including encounters with forecasted severe weather using flight information services broadcast (FIS\u2013B);\n**(8)**\nthe effort of the Administrator to modernize the air traffic control system, including timelines, technologies being incorporated, changes to operational rules, and training requirements;\n**(9)**\nthe role of air traffic controllers in ensuring aircraft separation, including the need for additional training to air traffic controllers given the requirements of this section;\n**(10)**\nthe necessity of certification for implementing collision prevention technology based on type of aircraft and operation;\n**(11)**\nthe capacity of the aerospace supply chain to manufacture necessary equipment;\n**(12)**\nthe use of existing air traffic control deviation authorization tools to implement the requirement in subsection (g)(2);\n**(13)**\nthe requirements for the final rule as specified in subsection (d);\n**(14)**\nif available at the time of consideration, the results of the studies on ADS\u2013B Out equipage and development of low-cost voluntary ADS\u2013B as required by sections 808 and 810 of FAA Reauthorization Act of 2024 ( Public Law 118\u201363 ); and\n**(15)**\nany other considerations the Administrator determines appropriate.\n##### (d) Requirements for final rule\nIn issuing the final rule required under subsection (a), the Administrator shall\u2014\n**(1)**\nestablish performance requirements for equipping collision prevention technology that, as determined by the Administrator, are appropriate for the covered aircraft and the operations, including the operating environment;\n**(2)**\nin establishing the performance requirements described in paragraph (1)\u2014\n**(A)**\nrequire such technology be configured to provide visual and audible alerting to the pilot and flight crew;\n**(B)**\nconsider the field of view of the pilots, human factors, and, if applicable, mounting method of such technology, to ensure that such technology can be readily utilized and has minimal risk of unexpected detachment;\n**(C)**\nconsider the reliability and resiliency of alerts in environments where inputs or signals, including GPS, can be jammed or spoofed; and\n**(D)**\nconsider the utilization of existing antenna locations or the placement of new antenna used to receive and, if applicable, transmit, data used in collision prevention technology;\n**(3)**\nidentify existing or issue additional relevant guidance or technical standard orders to carry out the requirements of this section; and\n**(4)**\nestablish an effective date not later than December 31, 2031, for equipping the covered aircraft with technology described in subsection (a) that reflects various aircraft types, appropriate maintenance cycles, and required updates to appropriate guidance for such technology after certification of such technologies.\n##### (e) Equivalent level of safety\nIn issuing the final rule required under this section, the Administrator shall allow for the use of any collision prevention technology (including technology that uses portable ADS\u2013B In receivers or other equipment that displays on an existing or future portable device, electronic flight bag, or panel mounted display) available for use at the time of the effective date established in subsection (d)(4), if the Administrator determines it provides an equivalent level of safety as the requirements of the final rule issued pursuant to subsection (a).\n##### (f) Technical assistance\nThe Administrator shall provide technical assistance to facilitating equipage across the entire fleet of affected aircraft to provide support for affected aircraft operators in complying with the requirements of this section.\n##### (g) Covered aircraft defined\nIn this section, the term covered aircraft \u2014\n**(1)**\nmeans any non-military aircraft, except a selected aircraft as defined in section 102, that is required to be equipped with ADS\u2013B Out under section 91.225 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations; and\n**(2)**\nexcludes aircraft that have a limited category special airworthiness certificate or an experimental airworthiness certificate, provided the pilot of such aircraft is authorized to deviate from the requirements of this section by air traffic control in the same manner ADS\u2013B Out deviations are approved under section 91.225(g) of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations.\n#### 105. Prohibition on certain use of ADS\u2013B data\n##### (a) In general\n**(1) Limitation on use of data**\nData from Automatic Dependent Surveillance\u2013Broadcast may not be used by any person, governmental agency, or other entity to identify aircraft for the purpose of obtaining revenue from the owner or operator of such aircraft, without the consent of such owner or operator.\n**(2) Use of data by air traffic controller**\nAutomatic Dependent Surveillance\u2013Broadcast data may be used to assist air traffic controllers in tracking aircraft and improving air traffic safety and efficiency.\n##### (b) Limit on use of ADS\u2013B data\nSection 46101(c)(1) of title 49, United States Code, is amended by striking the Administrator of the Federal Aviation Administration may not and inserting neither the Administrator of the Federal Aviation Administration nor any other Federal, State, local, territorial, or Tribal official may .\n#### 106. Rulemaking accountability\n##### (a) Public dashboard\nThe Secretary shall establish, maintain, and make available, on a publicly available website of the Department of Transportation, a dashboard that displays, for the rulemakings required in sections 102, 103, and 104\u2014\n**(1)**\ndates of publication and links to the minimum operating performance standards referenced by and developed pursuant to such sections;\n**(2)**\nthe date of establishment, membership roster, and tasking memoranda (or similar document) for rulemaking committees established pursuant to such sections;\n**(3)**\ndeadlines and actual dates for the submission for all required rulemaking committee reports to the Administrator or Congress;\n**(4)**\npublication dates of and a link to any\u2014\n**(A)**\nadvanced notice of proposed rulemakings published pursuant to such sections;\n**(B)**\nnotice of proposed rulemakings published pursuant to such sections; and\n**(C)**\nrevised notice of proposed rulemakings published pursuant to rulemakings described in subparagraphs (A) and (B);\n**(5)**\nthe opening and closing of public comment periods and a link to public comments;\n**(6)**\nthe publication of and a link to any final rule issued pursuant to such sections;\n**(7)**\nall associated official correspondence with the National Transportation Safety Board regarding related safety recommendations; and\n**(8)**\nany additional information the Secretary determines will increase transparency without delaying the publication of a final rule.\n##### (b) Congressional and family briefing\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, and every 180 days thereafter until the final rules required pursuant to sections 102, 103, and 104 are issued, the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress and the families of the victims of the midair collision referenced in National Transportation Safety Board Aviation Investigation Report AIR\u201326\u201302 adopted on January 27, 2026 on the progress in issuing such final rules.\n##### (c) Congressional oversight in case of failure to meet deadlines\n**(1) In general**\nIf the Administrator fails to meet any rulemaking deadline established in sections 102, 103, and 104, the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress in person not later than 4 weeks after the date on which such deadline is not met.\n**(2) Deadline for initial outreach and coordination**\nNot later than 4 days after the date described in paragraph (1), the Administrator shall begin initial outreach to and coordination with the appropriate committees of Congress to arrange and organize logistics of the briefing required under paragraph (1).\n**(3) Format and time of briefing**\nThe briefing required under paragraph (1) shall be in a format and at a time to be determined by the appropriate committees of Congress.\n#### 107. Time-on-position limits\n##### (a) Time-on-position limits\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator, in coordination with organizations representing air traffic controller managers and supervisors, shall establish time-on-position limits for operations supervisory personnel.\n**(2) Considerations**\nIn developing the limits described in paragraph (1), the Administrator shall\u2014\n**(A)**\nevaluate appropriate time-on-position limits for operations supervisory personnel, prioritizing the evaluation of such limits at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport and other air traffic facilities with high volumes of mixed rotorcraft and airplane traffic;\n**(B)**\nestablish such limits for Air Traffic Organization operations supervisory personnel at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport and other air traffic facilities with high volumes of mixed helicopter and airplane traffic;\n**(C)**\ndevelop guidance for district and facility-level management to adapt such limits to account for their own staffing and local standard operating procedures;\n**(D)**\nconsider the operational needs and staffing levels of the air traffic facilities described in the previous subparagraphs to ensure effective oversight and monitoring of safety critical operations;\n**(E)**\nconsider air traffic control specialists performing watch supervision in the controller-in-charge position;\n**(F)**\nconsider requirements of FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration , issued on February 20, 2025, or any successor document, and FAA Order JO 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control , issued on February 20, 2025, or any successor document;\n**(G)**\nconsider data, reports, and best practices pertaining to human factors; and\n**(H)**\nconsider any other items determined appropriate by the Administrator.\n**(3) Consultation**\nThe Administrator may consult with the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code.\n##### (b) Rule of construction\nNothing in this section shall be construed to interfere with any agreement between a governmental agency and the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code, section 7106(a) of title 5, United States Code, or section 40122 of title 49, United States Code.\n##### (c) Definitions\nIn this section:\n**(1) Controller-in-charge**\nThe term controller-in-charge means the bargaining unit air traffic control specialist responsible for providing watch supervision for the continuous operation of an air traffic control facility or area in any case in which operations supervisory personnel are not available.\n**(2) Operational oversight**\nThe term operational oversight means the duty of the individual in charge of the operation to effectively lead and manage the delivery of air traffic services by maintaining intentional engagement, situational awareness, and accountability within the area of supervision.\n**(3) Operations supervisory personnel**\nThe term operations supervisory personnel means managerial personnel responsible for the direct supervision of air traffic control operational personnel.\n#### 108. Controller threat and error management training\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 9 months after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall, in coordination with the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code, develop and implement initial, recurrent, and refresher training for air traffic controllers on threat and error management that is instructor-led and scenario-based.\n##### (b) Consultation\nIn developing the training under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consult with representatives of\u2014\n**(1)**\norganizations representing air traffic control managers and operations supervisors;\n**(2)**\naviation safety experts with specific knowledge of\u2014\n**(A)**\nhuman factors and human decision making in realistic operational settings; and\n**(B)**\nthreat and error management best practices and policies; and\n**(3)**\na career representative from the National Transportation Safety Board with subject matter expertise as an observer.\n##### (c) Considerations\nIn developing the training described in subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider, at a minimum\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe findings and recommendations of the National Transportation Safety Board, including as contained in the final aviation investigation report, AIR\u201326\u201302, adopted on January 27, 2026, such as\u2014\n**(A)**\ntraining controllers to continuously monitor their environment to more quickly and accurately identify threats;\n**(B)**\npromoting team communication to ensure that communications are clear, timely, and assertive;\n**(C)**\nemphasizing effective scanning habits;\n**(D)**\nrecognizing patterns in the development of adverse events; and\n**(E)**\nenhanced decision making under stress by developing habits that balance procedural compliance with problem-solving;\n**(2)**\nthe requirements of\u2014\n**(A)**\nFAA Order JO 3120.4S, titled Air Traffic Technical Training , issued on August 28, 2024;\n**(B)**\nFAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration , issued on February 20, 2025;\n**(C)**\nFAA Order JO 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control , issued on February 20, 2025; and\n**(D)**\nother relevant air traffic control standards, guidance, and policies;\n**(3)**\nthe frequency of the recurrent and refresher training described in subsection (a) and whether frequency should be increased for air traffic controllers in facilities managing high-complexity or high-volume airspace;\n**(4)**\ndata, reports, and peer-reviewed studies on human factors and threat and error management best practices;\n**(5)**\nthe appropriate use of tower simulator systems and other advanced training technologies to supplement the recurrent training described in subsection (a), including the use of data analytics from such systems and technologies to individualize instruction;\n**(6)**\nthe use of data analytics to identify systemic gaps in the recurrent and refresher training described in subsection (a) and to dynamically enhance training curriculum and techniques;\n**(7)**\ndata gathered from aviation safety reporting programs; and\n**(8)**\nany other item determined appropriate by the Administrator.\n##### (d) Implementation\nNot later than 90 days after the development of the training under subsection (a), the Administrator shall revise the orders of the FAA described in subsection (c)(2), or any successor documents, and any corresponding policy or guidance materials, to reflect the requirements of this section.\n##### (e) Briefing to Congress\nNot later than 1 year after the training requirements under this section and section 109 are established, the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on the implementation of such training and any potential recommendations for improvements.\n##### (f) Threat and error management defined\nIn this section, the term threat and error management has the meaning described in chapter 6 of the Risk Management Handbook (FAA H\u20138083\u20132A) or any successor document.\n#### 109. Controller visual separation training\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 270 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall, in coordination with the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code, develop and implement initial, recurrent, and refresher training for air traffic controllers on tower-applied and pilot-applied visual separation procedures that is instructor-led and scenario-based.\n##### (b) Consultation\nIn developing and implementing the training required under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consult with representatives of\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe certified bargaining representative of aviation safety inspectors and engineers for the FAA;\n**(2)**\norganizations representing certified collective bargaining representatives of airline pilots;\n**(3)**\norganizations representing air traffic control managers and supervisors;\n**(4)**\norganizations representing general aviation pilots; and\n**(5)**\naviation safety experts with specific knowledge of\u2014\n**(A)**\nhuman factors and human decision making in realistic operational settings; and\n**(B)**\ntower-applied and pilot-applied visual separation procedures and regulations.\n##### (c) Considerations\nIn developing the training under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider, at a minimum\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe findings and recommendations made by the National Transportation Safety Board, including as contained in the final aviation investigation report, AIR\u201326\u201302, adopted on January 27, 2026;\n**(2)**\nthe requirements of\u2014\n**(A)**\nFAA Order JO 3120.4S, titled Air Traffic Technical Training , issued on August 28, 2024;\n**(B)**\nFAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration , issued on February 20, 2025;\n**(C)**\nFAA Order JO 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control , issued on February 20, 2025; and\n**(D)**\nother relevant air traffic control standards, guidance, and policies;\n**(3)**\nthe frequency of the recurrent and refresher training described in subsection (a), including\u2014\n**(A)**\nwhether such frequency should be increased for air traffic controllers in facilities managing high-complexity or high-volume airspace; and\n**(B)**\nthe need for advance training and guidance ahead of any changes to FAA visual separation policies;\n**(4)**\nthe appropriate use of tower simulator systems and other advanced training technologies to supplement the recurrent and refresher training described in subsection (a), including the use of data analytics from such systems and technologies to individualize instruction;\n**(5)**\nthe use of data analytics to identify systemic gaps in the recurrent and refresher training described in subsection (a) and to dynamically enhance training curriculum and techniques;\n**(6)**\ndata gathered from aviation safety reporting programs; and\n**(7)**\nany other item determined appropriate by the Administrator.\n##### (d) Implementation\nNot later than 90 days after the development of the training under subsection (a), the Administrator shall revise the orders of the FAA described in subparagraph (c)(2), or any successor documents, and any corresponding policy or guidance materials, to reflect the requirements of this section.\n#### 110. Safety risk assessment tool\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall develop a safety risk assessment tool for use by air traffic controllers, including by supervisory air traffic control personnel, to assist in airspace risk identification, mitigation, and operational decision making.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn carrying out subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider, at a minimum\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe development of a safety risk assessment tool capable of supporting air traffic controllers in\u2014\n**(A)**\nidentifying safety risks;\n**(B)**\nanalyzing the impact of and prioritizing such risks; and\n**(C)**\ndeveloping strategies to reduce or eliminate such risks in real time;\n**(2)**\ndata, reports, studies, and best practices on threat and error management;\n**(3)**\nfindings and recommendations of the\u2014\n**(A)**\nNational Transportation Safety Board, including as contained in the final aviation investigation report, AIR\u201326\u201302, adopted on January 27, 2026;\n**(B)**\nNational Airspace System Safety Review Team as contained in the final report titled Discussion and Recommendations to Address Risk in the National Airspace System , issued on November 15, 2023; and\n**(C)**\nfrontline manager workload study authorized under section 412 of the FAA Reauthorization Act of 2024 ( Public Law 118\u201363 );\n**(4)**\nair traffic facility type and staffing level;\n**(5)**\nrisk assessment guidance, policies, and regulations of the Administration in place prior to the date of enactment of this Act;\n**(6)**\ndata gathered from aviation safety reporting programs;\n**(7)**\nbest practices or similar relevant risk assessment tools and methods used by foreign civil aviation authorities;\n**(8)**\nthe feasibility of leveraging commercially available products or technologies that may be utilized to develop such tool;\n**(9)**\nbenefits of incorporating such tool into a Common Automation Platform; and\n**(10)**\nany other factors determined relevant by the Administrator.\n##### (c) Coordination\nIn developing the safety risk assessment tool under subsection (a), the Administrator shall coordinate with\u2014\n**(1)**\norganizations representing air traffic control supervisors and managers;\n**(2)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(3)**\naviation safety experts with specific knowledge of threat and error management;\n**(4)**\naviation safety experts with specific knowledge of human factors and human decision making in realistic operational settings;\n**(5)**\norganizations representing operators of Federal contract towers pursuant to section 47124 of title 49, United States Code; and\n**(6)**\nany other stakeholders determined relevant by the Administrator.\n##### (d) Briefing to Congress\nNot later than 18 months after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe development of the safety risk assessment tool required under this section and recommendations for implementation;\n**(2)**\nthe progress of implementation described in subsection (e); and\n**(3)**\nany recommendations to improve the deployment of the safety risk assessment tool.\n##### (e) Implementation\nThe Administrator shall deploy the safety risk assessment tool developed under this section at\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport air traffic control tower, not later than 1 year after the development of the safety risk assessment tool;\n**(2)**\nair traffic control facilities with high volumes of mixed rotorcraft and airplane traffic not later than 18 months after the development of the safety risk assessment tool; and\n**(3)**\nany remaining air traffic control facilities not later than 2 years after the development of the safety risk assessment tool.\n##### (f) Threat and error management defined\nIn this section, the term threat and error management has the meaning described in chapter 6 of the Risk Management Handbook (FAA H\u20138083\u20132A) or any successor document.\n#### 111. Operational rates at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 30 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall initiate an assessment of the aircraft arrival rate at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn conducting the assessment described in subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nairspace complexity;\n**(2)**\nairfield limitations;\n**(3)**\nmixed-fleet operations;\n**(4)**\ntraffic volume;\n**(5)**\nair carrier scheduling practices;\n**(6)**\nthe operational capacity of such airport;\n**(7)**\nthe current hourly instrument flight rules allocation practice at such airport;\n**(8)**\nexpertise provided by the Air Traffic Organization; and\n**(9)**\nany other considerations the Administrator determines appropriate.\n##### (c) Completion of assessment\nNot later than 180 days after the Administrator initiates the assessment under subsection (a), the Administrator shall complete and submit to the appropriate committees of Congress such assessment, including any related findings and recommendations.\n##### (d) Rulemaking\nNot later than 30 days after completing the assessment pursuant to subsection (c), and taking such assessment into account, the Administrator shall initiate a rulemaking proceeding to update subpart K of part 93 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, to require allocated instrument flight rules operations at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport to be prescribed in periods not greater than 30 minutes to ensure such airport does not exceed safe capacity.\n##### (e) Consultation\nIn conducting the rulemaking required under subsection (d), the Administrator shall consult with the following:\n**(1)**\nAny air carrier operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, with scheduled operations at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport, including regional air carriers and low-cost and ultra-low-cost air carriers.\n**(2)**\nAir carriers operating under parts 91, including subpart K, and 135 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, authorized to conduct non-scheduled operations at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport.\n**(3)**\nThe exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United Sates Code.\n**(4)**\nThe Metropolitan Washington Airports Authority.\n**(5)**\nAny other stakeholders the Administrator determines appropriate.\n#### 112. Time-based flow management\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall implement operational use of the time-based flow management system at Potomac Consolidated Terminal Radar Approach Control and associated air traffic control towers.\n#### 113. Air traffic control facility levels\n##### (a) Review of air traffic control facility level criteria\n**(1) In general**\nThe Administrator and the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code, (in this section referred to as the Parties ) may, at their joint election, review and advise, as agreed to, the criteria and procedures used to assess, determine, and validate the facility pay levels of air traffic control facilities.\n**(2) Considerations**\nIn conducting a review under paragraph (1), the Parties may consider\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe many variables that may affect the difficulty and complexity of air traffic control work, including technological advancements, aviation industry trends, and the modification or extension of air traffic control services;\n**(B)**\nweights and add-ons used to calculate the traffic count index and other related formulas for air traffic control facilities; and\n**(C)**\nwhether new weights and add-ons should be incorporated into such formulas to more accurately reflect the air traffic density and complexity of the facility operations.\n##### (b) Reassessment of air traffic control facility levels\n**(1) Limitation**\nNo changes to facility pay levels due to data source changes may be implemented until negotiations pursuant to the collective bargaining agreement of the Parties and title 49, United States Code, have been completed.\n**(2) Application of standard**\nUpon completion of a review conducted under subsection (a) and related negotiations pursuant to the collective bargaining agreement of the Parties and title 49, United States Code, the Parties shall apply the standard in accordance with any agreements made pursuant to this section at\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport; and\n**(B)**\nall other air traffic control facilities, prioritizing facilities with high volumes of mixed rotorcraft and airplane traffic.\n##### (c) Rule of construction\nNothing in this section may be construed to interfere with any agreement between a governmental agency and the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code, or section 40122 of title 49, United States Code.\n#### 114. Working group to evaluate shared frequency around Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 3 months after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall convene a working group (in this section referred to as the Working Group ) to conduct a comprehensive evaluation of the safety benefits and risks of requiring all aircraft to use the same communications frequency during any period in which helicopter and local air traffic control positions are combined in the Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport air traffic control tower.\n##### (b) Members\nThe Working Group convened under subsection (a) shall be comprised of representatives of\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(2)**\nthe organization representing air traffic control operational supervisors and managers;\n**(3)**\nnot fewer than 3 separate organizations representing the certified collective bargaining representatives of pilots operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(4)**\nair medical services;\n**(5)**\nan organization representing helicopter aviation operators and pilots;\n**(6)**\nan organization representing business aviation operators and pilots;\n**(7)**\nair carriers operating under part 121 of title 14, United States Code;\n**(8)**\nan individual that has expertise in an operational or academic discipline that is relevant to the analysis of human factors in aviation, which may include air carrier operations, line pilot expertise, air traffic control, linguistics, human-machine integration, general aviation operations, and organizational behavior and culture;\n**(9)**\nthe FAA, provided the representative has expertise on flight operations in the area described in subsection (a);\n**(10)**\nthe Department of Defense, provided the representative has expertise on Department of Defense flight operations in the area described in subsection (a);\n**(11)**\nthe Coast Guard, provided the representative has expertise on Coast Guard flight operations in the area described in subsection (a);\n**(12)**\nthe National Transportation Safety Board; and\n**(13)**\nother organizations or agencies as determined necessary by the Administrator.\n##### (c) Local operator preference\nThe members described in paragraphs (3), (4), (5), (6), and (7) of subsection (b) shall be, or represent, individuals who operate in the Washington, DC Metropolitan Area Special Flight Rules Area, as defined in subpart V of part 93 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations.\n##### (d) Government representatives\nThe members described in paragraphs (11), (12), (13), (14), and, in the case of a representative chosen by the Administrator that is from a governmental agency, (15) of subsection (b)\u2014\n**(1)**\nmay not be political appointees; and\n**(2)**\nshall be nonvoting members of the Working Group.\n##### (e) Duration\n**(1) In general**\nMembers of the Working Group shall be appointed for the duration of the Working Group.\n**(2) Length of existence**\n**(A) In general**\nThe Working Group shall have an initial duration of 1 year.\n**(B) Optional extension**\nThe Administrator may extend the duration of the Working Group for an additional period of up to 1 year.\n##### (f) Considerations\nIn conducting the comprehensive evaluation under subsection (a), the Working Group shall, at minimum, consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe benefits or detriments to pilot and air traffic controller situation awareness;\n**(2)**\nto the greatest extent possible, the human factors that would impact pilot and air traffic controller situation awareness;\n**(3)**\nto the greatest extent possible, the human factors that would impact pilot and air traffic controllers during critical phases of flight;\n**(4)**\nexisting products by other working groups related to human factors in aviation safety;\n**(5)**\npilot training requirements;\n**(6)**\nair traffic controller training requirements;\n**(7)**\nif any, technological limitations or challenges that would impede aircraft from using the same communications frequency;\n**(8)**\nthe potential for overlapping, conflicting, and simultaneous communication transmissions, prior to and after any improvements made as a result of the assessment conducted pursuant to section 115;\n**(9)**\nthe potential for misdirected, missed, or stepped on communications if requiring all aircraft to use the same communication frequency;\n**(10)**\nNational Transportation Safety Board recommendations pertaining to miscommunications on crowded frequencies, including relevant recommendations included in the National Transportation Safety Board Aviation Investigation Report AIR\u201326\u201302 adopted on January 27, 2026; and\n**(11)**\nsolicited feedback from air carriers operating under part 121 and part 135 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, and general aviation operators under part 91 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations.\n##### (g) Report\nNot later than 6 months after the conclusion of the Working Group, the Working Group shall submit to the Administrator and the appropriate committees of Congress a report on the findings and recommendations resulting from the activities carried out under this section.\n##### (h) Implementation\nNot later than 6 months after receiving recommendations outlined in the report under subsection (g), the Administrator shall operationally validate such recommendations and may take such action, as appropriate, to implement such recommendations.\n#### 115. Anti-blocking technology\n##### (a) Assessment\nNot later than 30 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall initiate an assessment on the feasibility, maturity, hazards, and safety benefits of technology that serves to alert air traffic controllers or flight crews to instances of potentially blocked transmissions when simultaneous broadcasting occurs.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn conducting the assessment under subsection (a), the Administrator shall, at minimum, consider\u2014\n**(1)**\ntechnologies currently in use domestically and internationally that alert an air traffic controller or flight crew to instances in which radio transmissions may have been blocked;\n**(2)**\nthe technical standards written for, and associated with, the use of such technologies identified under paragraph (1);\n**(3)**\nexisting and proposed technologies not in use that could alert an air traffic controller or flight crew to instances in which radio transmissions may have been blocked;\n**(4)**\nthe technical standards that would be needed to implement the technologies identified under paragraph (3);\n**(5)**\nthe potential benefits and enhanced awareness that the adoption of such technologies would provide;\n**(6)**\nthe technological limitations associated with such technologies;\n**(7)**\nair traffic controller training requirements;\n**(8)**\nthe effort of the FAA to modernize the air traffic control system, including timelines, the incorporation of new technologies, and planned training; and\n**(9)**\nany benefits and detriments to air traffic controller situational awareness, including availability of information, nuisance alerts, and human factors.\n##### (c) Consultation\nIn conducting the assessment under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consult with stakeholders or standards organizations, including\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(2)**\nthe organization representing air traffic control operational supervisors and managers;\n**(3)**\nthe certified bargaining representative of aviation safety inspectors and engineers for the FAA;\n**(4)**\nan organization representing manufacturers of air traffic management systems, equipment and technologies;\n**(5)**\nan organization representing helicopter aviation operators and pilots;\n**(6)**\nan organization representing general aviation operators and pilots; and\n**(7)**\nany other organization or agency the Administrator determines appropriate.\n##### (d) Report\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report on the results of the assessment under subsection (a) that includes\u2014\n**(1)**\na list of technologies identified by the Administrator serving the purpose described in subsection (a);\n**(2)**\na list of technologies the Administrator proposes that could serve the purpose described in subsection (a);\n**(3)**\nresults of simulations and testing; and\n**(4)**\na plan to implement the technologies listed under paragraphs (1) and (2) if the assessment under subsection (a) finds such technology can be safely implemented, including\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe scope of potential upgrades;\n**(B)**\npredicted costs;\n**(C)**\na projected timeline; and\n**(D)**\nhow the potential upgrades to facilities and equipment within the scope of subparagraph (A) would be prioritized.\n#### 116. Task force to identify improvements to air traffic controller conflict alert system\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 3 months after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall convene a task force (in this section referred to as the Task Force ) to develop a framework detailing the priorities, goals, timeline, and recommendations to implement improvements to the conflict alert system to provide more salient and meaningful alerts to air traffic controllers based on the severity of the conflict triggering the alert.\n##### (b) Members\nThe Task Force convened under subsection (a) shall be comprised of representatives of\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(2)**\nthe organization representing air traffic control operational supervisors and managers;\n**(3)**\nthe organization representing operators under the Contract Tower Program established under section 47124 of title 49, United States Code;\n**(4)**\nthe certified bargaining representative of aviation safety inspectors and engineers for the FAA;\n**(5)**\nindividuals with expertise in the human factors of alert design and related impacts on human performance;\n**(6)**\nindividuals with expertise in an operational or academic discipline that is relevant to the analysis of human factors in aviation, which may include air carrier operations, line pilot expertise, air traffic control, linguistics, human-machine integration, general aviation operations, and organizational behavior and culture;\n**(7)**\nthe FAA, including the Air Traffic Organization and the Office of Finance and Management, provided such representative has expertise on equipment procurement; and\n**(8)**\nother organizations or agencies as determined necessary by the Administrator.\n##### (c) Voting\nThe members described in paragraphs (3), (6), and, in the case of a representative chosen by the Administrator that is from a governmental agency, (7) of subsection (b) shall be nonvoting members of the Task Force.\n##### (d) Duration\n**(1) In general**\nMembers of the Task Force shall be appointed for the duration of the Task Force.\n**(2) Length of existence**\n**(A) In general**\nThe Task Force shall have an initial duration of 1 year.\n**(B) Optional extension**\nThe Administrator may extend the duration of the Task Force for an additional period of up to 6 months.\n##### (e) Considerations\nIn developing the framework under subsection (a), the Task Force shall, at minimum, consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe benefits and detriments to air traffic controller situational awareness, including availability of information, nuisance and false alerts, and human factors;\n**(2)**\nopportunities and challenges of consolidating numerous systems and underlying data sources into a single display, including through the deployment of the Enterprise-Information Display System;\n**(3)**\nexisting products by other working groups related to human factors in aviation safety;\n**(4)**\nair traffic controller training requirements;\n**(5)**\nadvances in available technology not being utilized as of the date on which the Task Force is convened;\n**(6)**\ntechnological limitations;\n**(7)**\nNational Transportation Safety Board recommendations pertaining to air traffic controller alerts, distractions, and loss of focus;\n**(8)**\nthe effort of the FAA to modernize the air traffic control system, including timelines, new technologies being incorporated, and planned training; and\n**(9)**\nsolicited feedback from equipment manufacturers and entities involved with the air traffic control modernization effort of the Administrator.\n##### (f) Report\nNot later than 4 months after the conclusion of the Task Force, the Task Force shall submit to the Administrator and the appropriate committees of Congress a report that includes the framework developed as a result of the activities carried out under subsection (a).\n##### (g) Implementation plan\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 8 months after receiving the framework outlined in the report under subsection (f), the Administrator shall finalize and submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a plan (in this section referred to as the Plan ) to implement such framework.\n**(2) Contents**\nSuch Plan shall include, as appropriate\u2014\n**(A)**\nspecific training requirements for air traffic controllers, as detailed in\u2014\n**(i)**\nFAA Order JO 3120.4S, titled Air Traffic Technical Training , issued on August 28, 2024;\n**(ii)**\nFAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration , issued on February 20, 2025; and\n**(iii)**\nany successor or other relevant documents or guidance; and\n**(B)**\na publicly available prioritized list of airports enumerating the order in which they will receive such upgrades.\n**(3) Time limit**\nThe Plan may not contain a timeline of implementation that exceeds 2 years.\n##### (h) Implementation\nThe Administrator shall immediately begin implementing the Plan upon the submission of such Plan under subsection (g)(1) to the appropriate committees of Congress.\n##### (i) Briefings to Congress\nNot later than 6 months after the submission of the Plan to the appropriate committees of Congress under subsection (g)(1), and every 6 months thereafter until the full implementation of the Plan, the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on the progress of implementation.\n#### 117. Postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing\n##### (a) Sense of Congress\nThe Administrator shall abide by DOT Order 3910.1D, titled Drug and Alcohol-Free Departmental Workplace Program (or any successor document) to ensure appropriate postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing.\n##### (b) Revision of procedures\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall revise procedures of the Air Traffic Organization to ensure an appropriate on-site supervisor makes each postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing determination in a timely manner based on an assessment of such supervisor of whether the event meets testing criteria and which controllers had duties pertaining to the involved aircraft without need to wait for investigation or approval.\n##### (c) Training\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall incorporate training on the revised postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing determination procedure described in subsection (b) for all staff of the Air Traffic Organization who have responsibilities under such procedure.\n**(2) Requirements**\nThe training described under this subsection shall, at a minimum\u2014\n**(A)**\nbe administered during initial training, and annually thereafter; and\n**(B)**\ninclude a postlearning knowledge assessment.\n##### (d) Review\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, and annually thereafter, the Secretary shall conduct a review of the ability of each FAA-operated air traffic control facility to routinely accomplish the required postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing within the Secretary\u2019s specified timeframes of within 2 hours for alcohol testing and within 4 hours for drug testing.\n**(2) Requirements**\nThe review described under this subsection shall, at a minimum, require each FAA-operated air traffic control facility to conduct a demonstration to establish the time that would be required for urine and breath evidence collection to begin if testing were unexpectedly needed during a time with the lowest routinely anticipated level of resource availability for testing.\n**(3) Remediation**\nAfter each review under paragraph (1), the Administrator shall work with the Secretary to mitigate identified barriers to timely postaccident and postincident drug and alcohol testing, and to remediate the performance of each facility for which the demonstration under paragraph (2) indicated inability to meet required timeframes for postaccident drug or alcohol testing.\n**(4) Report**\nNot later than 3 months after each review under paragraph (1), the Secretary shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report detailing the results of the review, including facilities in need of remediation, progress at facilities previously identified for remediation, and planned approaches to remediation.\n#### 118. Further modifications to Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport area helicopter routes\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 90 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall evaluate, via the safety risk management process in accordance with FAA Order JO 8040.4C, titled Safety Risk Management Policy (or any successor document), charted helicopter routes in the vicinity of Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport.\n##### (b) Revisions to deconflict traffic\nUpon the completion of each route evaluation under subsection (a), the Administrator shall immediately, as necessary, revise such route to ensure that the route and routes utilized by fixed-wing aircraft\u2014\n**(1)**\nare safely deconflicted physically at all times; or\n**(2)**\nhave operating procedures that require positive control from the controller to ensure safe deconfliction during operations.\n##### (c) Safety review requirements\nIn carrying out the route revisions required under subsection (b), the Administrator shall conduct a safety risk management review, as necessary, for any helicopter route changes, in accordance with FAA Order 8040.4C, titled Safety Risk Management Policy (or any successor document).\n##### (d) Report\nNot later than 120 days after the Administrator completes all the evaluations and subsequent route revisions required under this section, the Administrator shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report containing\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe results of the evaluations required under subsection (a);\n**(2)**\nthe route revisions required under subsection (b), including an explanation for such revisions; and\n**(3)**\nthe safety risk management review documentation developed as a result of the review conducted under subsection (c).\n#### 119. Requiring vertical separation near airports during critical phases of flight\n##### (a) In general\nExcept as provided in subsection (b), the Administrator shall ensure that each segment of a helicopter route contains, in the appropriate helicopter route chart, recommended flight altitudes, including altitude ceilings and floors, in a manner consistent with FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document).\n##### (b) Consideration of vertical separation in route criteria\nNot later than 60 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall amend FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document), to add minimum vertical separation requirements to the criteria for the helicopter route chart program.\n##### (c) Charting minimum separation near airports\n**(1) In general**\nThe Administrator shall ensure that any helicopter chart that represents an area near an airport clearly conveys to an operator the segments of such helicopter routes in the vicinity of such airport.\n**(2) Content requirements**\nAt minimum, each such chart shall clearly convey for each of the segments, the recommended flight altitudes, including altitude ceilings and floors, and any necessary instructions, to convey minimum separation, in accordance with FAA Order JO 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control (or any successor document), between\u2014\n**(A)**\na helicopter or powered-lift aircraft utilizing such segment; and\n**(B)**\na fixed-wing aircraft operating at or near such airport during critical phases of flight.\n##### (d) Update policy\nNot later than 90 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall update FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document), to account for any additional changes made by this section.\n##### (e) Annual review\nThe Administrator shall ensure that any changes made to Helicopter Route Charts as a result of this section are assessed on an annual basis as part of the annual review described in section 120.\n#### 120. Helicopter Route Chart annual review\n##### (a) Criteria review\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, and annually thereafter, the Administrator shall initiate a review of the criteria for annual reviews of helicopter routes as required pursuant to FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document).\n**(2) Update of criteria**\nAfter each annual criteria review under paragraph (1), the Administrator shall update the criteria based on such review and publish the updated criteria on a publicly available website of the FAA.\n**(3) Changes to route reviews**\nAfter any change is made to FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document) pursuant to section 119(d), the Administrator shall update the criteria for annual reviews of helicopter routes to reflect such change.\n##### (b) Publication\nThe Administrator shall publish, on a publicly available website of the FAA, the date on which the annual review for each Helicopter Route Chart has been most recently completed, as required pursuant to FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration (or any successor document).\n##### (c) Report\nNot later than December 31, 2026, and December 31 of each year thereafter, the Administrator shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report containing, at a minimum, the following information:\n**(1)**\nA summary of changes, if applicable, made to each Helicopter Route Chart, including\u2014\n**(A)**\nchanges, additions, or deletions to designated helicopter routes;\n**(B)**\nchanges in instrument flight rules routes;\n**(C)**\nadditions or deletions of visual checkpoints; and\n**(D)**\nrationale or safety data to justify any changes described in subparagraphs (A) through (C).\n**(2)**\nThe safety risk management documentation completed in accordance with FAA Order JO 8040.4C, titled Safety Risk Management Policy (or any successor document).\n**(3)**\nA summary of any advanced consultation between the Administrator and impacted helicopter and fixed-wing operators in planning the safety risk management process.\n**(4)**\nA certification that the designated recommended route altitudes and flight ceilings and floors ensure helicopters maintain minimum separation, in accordance with FAA Order 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control (or any successor document), with fixed-wing aircraft operating along airport approach and departure paths.\n##### (d) Failure To submit\n**(1) In general**\nIf the Administrator fails to submit an annual report required under subsection (b) on or before the date on which such report is required to be submitted, the Chief Operating Officer of the Air Traffic Organization shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress in person not later than 4 weeks after such date.\n**(2) Deadline for initial outreach and coordination**\nNot later than 4 days after such date, the FAA shall begin initial outreach to and coordination with the appropriate committees of Congress to arrange and organize logistics of the briefing required under paragraph (1).\n**(3) Format and time of briefing**\nThe briefing required under paragraph (1) shall be in a format and at a time to be determined by such committees.\n#### 121. Visual charts\n##### (a) Study\nNot later than 30 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall initiate a study on incorporating the lateral location and published altitudes of helicopter routes into all instrument and visual approach and departure procedures for airports to provide situation awareness to fixed-wing operators of the risk of helicopter traffic operating in the vicinity of such operators.\n##### (b) Consultation\nIn carrying out subsection (a), the Administrator shall consult with relevant stakeholders, including\u2014\n**(1)**\nair carriers;\n**(2)**\nan organization representing helicopter operators and pilots;\n**(3)**\nan organization representing general aviation operators and pilots;\n**(4)**\nan organization representing business aviation operators and pilots;\n**(5)**\nan organization representing emergency air medical services;\n**(6)**\nrepresentatives of the Department of Defense and United States Coast Guard who are not political appointees;\n**(7)**\nnot fewer than 3 separate organizations representing certified collective bargaining representatives of airline pilots operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(8)**\nthe certified exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code; and\n**(9)**\nan individual that has expertise in an operational or academic discipline that is relevant to the analysis of human factors in aviation, including air carrier operations, line pilot expertise, air traffic control, linguistics, human-machine integration, general aviation operations, and organizational behavior and culture.\n##### (c) Considerations\nIn carrying out subsection (a), the Administrator shall consider the\u2014\n**(1)**\nspacing and legibility of information on charts;\n**(2)**\nworkload of flight crews at lower altitudes and during critical phases of flight;\n**(3)**\nfeasibility and decipherability of layered information on digital charts;\n**(4)**\ncurrent best practices for pilots when landing at or departing from airports with high volume helicopter traffic but that do not have charted helicopter routes; and\n**(5)**\nhuman factors involved with approach and departure procedures.\n##### (d) Implementation\nNot later than 1 year after initiating the study under subsection (a), the Administrator shall make any revisions necessary to\u2014\n**(1)**\nTerminal Procedures Publications to include charted helicopter routes to provide appropriate situational awareness to fixed-wing operators; and\n**(2)**\nHelicopter Route Charts to include airport approach and departure paths to provide appropriate situational awareness to helicopter operators.\n##### (e) Congressional briefing\nIf the Administrator makes revisions under subsection (d), the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on such revisions not later than 60 days after making such revisions.\n#### 122. Close proximity encounters\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 60 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall establish a working group to make recommendations on\u2014\n**(1)**\nan objective definition of close proximity encounters;\n**(2)**\nassociated parameters that can be used to monitor the prevalence of such encounters and identify areas of potential traffic conflict for safety assurance and safety risk management for such encounters; and\n**(3)**\nmaking publicly available aggregated information about all such encounters, including date and location.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn carrying out subsection (a), the working group shall consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nexisting airborne separation rules and required loss of airborne separation reporting requirements;\n**(2)**\nthe development of a definition of, and associated parameters for, close proximity encounter events;\n**(3)**\ndata gathered from aviation safety reporting systems and reports, including the Aviation Safety Information Analysis and Sharing Program, the Aviation Safety Action Program, the Performance Data Analysis and Reporting System, the Aviation Risk Identification and Assessment ( ARIA ) system, preliminary ARIA reports, the Air Traffic Safety Action Program, the Aviation Safety Reporting System, the Near Midair Collision System, mandatory occurrence reports, and other relevant systems and reports;\n**(4)**\nNational Transportation Safety Board aviation investigation report AIR\u201326\u201302, adopted on January 27, 2026;\n**(5)**\nFAA risk assessment guidance, policies, and regulations in place prior to the date of enactment of this Act;\n**(6)**\nbest practices or similar relevant risk assessment tools and methods used by foreign civil aviation authorities; and\n**(7)**\nany other factors determined relevant by the working group.\n##### (c) Membership\nThe working group shall consist of the following:\n**(1) Appointed members**\nThe following members appointed by the Administrator:\n**(A)**\n2 representatives of the National Aeronautics and Space Administration with expertise in safety data.\n**(B)**\n5 appropriately qualified representatives of aviation labor organizations (designated by the applicable represented organization), including\u2014\n**(i)**\norganizations representing certified collective bargaining representatives of airline pilots;\n**(ii)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representatives of FAA air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(iii)**\norganizations representing helicopter operators and pilots, including law enforcement and air ambulance operators; and\n**(iv)**\norganizations representing general aviation operators and pilots.\n**(C)**\nNot fewer than 5 independent subject matter experts in safety management systems and safety data who\u2014\n**(i)**\nhave not served as a political appointee in the Administration; and\n**(ii)**\nhave a minimum of 10 years of relevant applied experience.\n**(D)**\n2 air carrier employees whose job responsibilities include administration of a safety management system.\n**(E)**\n2 individuals representing holders of a certificate issued under part 21 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, whose job responsibilities include administration of a safety management system.\n**(F)**\n2 other representatives from the aerospace industry that do not meet the criteria described in subparagraph (D) or (E) and who have expertise in safety assurance or safety risk or whose job responsibilities include administration of a safety management system.\n**(G)**\nA career representative from the National Transportation Safety Board with subject matter expertise, as a nonvoting member.\n**(2) Advisory members**\nIn addition to the appointed members described in paragraph (1), the working group shall be advised by up to 5 employees of the Administration, at least 3 of whom shall be subject matter experts in implementing safety assurance and safety risk management.\n##### (d) Implementation\nNot later than 30 days after the working group develops recommendations under subsection (a), the Administrator shall make publicly available a report containing the recommendations and describing how the Administrator will implement such recommendations.\n#### 123. Notification of close proximity encounters and analysis of data\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 180 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator, in accordance with the mandatory occurrence reporting requirements in FAA Order JO 7210.632A, titled Air Traffic Organization Occurrence Reporting (or any successor document), FAA Order 8020.11D, titled Aircraft Accident and Incident Notification, Investigation, and Reporting (or any successor document), and FAA Advisory Circular AC 90\u2013120, titled Operational Use of Airborne Collision Avoidance Systems (or any successor document), shall establish a process to\u2014\n**(1)**\nnotify, with respect to each event, parties involved with\u2014\n**(A)**\na near midair collision event;\n**(B)**\na traffic collision avoidance system resolution advisory event;\n**(C)**\na close proximity encounter, as defined pursuant to section 122; and\n**(D)**\nany other events, as determined by the Administrator; and\n**(2)**\nprovide deidentified event data to the Aviation Safety Information Analysis and Sharing program.\n##### (b) Requirements\nIn establishing the process under subsection (a), the Administrator shall\u2014\n**(1)**\nestablish a database that tracks the details of events described in subsection (a)(1);\n**(2)**\ncontinuously monitor and review such database to identify areas of potential traffic conflict for safety assurance and safety risk management;\n**(3)**\nensure timeliness of notifications to the parties described in subsection (a)(1) so that relevant data remains available before meaningful safety analysis, reporting, or corrective action is no longer practicable;\n**(4)**\nconsider informing, with deidentified or aggregated data, other frequent operators of events described in subsection (a)(1); and\n**(5)**\nconsider the practicality and usefulness of notification requirements for\u2014\n**(A)**\nairport surface loss of separation;\n**(B)**\nloss of separation with terrain or obstacles;\n**(C)**\nairborne loss of separation; and\n**(D)**\nany other close proximity encounters as determined by the Administrator.\n##### (c) Consultation\nIn establishing the process under subsection (a), the Administrator shall consult with\u2014\n**(1)**\nair carriers operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(2)**\nair carriers operating under part 135 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(3)**\nair carriers operating under part 91 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(4)**\norganizations representing helicopter aviation operators and pilots;\n**(5)**\norganizations representing the general aviation community;\n**(6)**\norganizations representing business aviation operators;\n**(7)**\norganizations representing experimental aircraft operators;\n**(8)**\norganizations representing powered-lift operators;\n**(9)**\norganizations representing certified collective bargaining representatives of airline pilots;\n**(10)**\nthe certified exclusive bargaining representatives of air traffic controllers of the Administration certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(11)**\nFAA subject matter experts, including aviation safety inspectors; and\n**(12)**\nother aviation safety experts determined appropriate by the Administrator.\n##### (d) Briefing\nNot later than 30 days after establishing the process required under subsection (a), the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on the implementation of this section.\n##### (e) Report\nNot later than 1 year after establishing the process required under subsection (a), and annually thereafter, the Administrator shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report containing\u2014\n**(1)**\ndata on number and location of\u2014\n**(A)**\nnear midair collision events;\n**(B)**\ntraffic collision avoidance system resolution advisory events; and\n**(C)**\nclose proximity encounters, as defined pursuant to section 122;\n**(2)**\nthe average time of notification to parties involved in such events;\n**(3)**\nidentified locations of concern or other trends; and\n**(4)**\nactions taken to mitigate identified risks and reduce such events.\n##### (f) Protection of data\n**(1) In general**\nData collected in response to subsection (a) shall be used solely for safety assurance and safety risk management.\n**(2) Consistency with existing safety programs**\nThe Administrator shall ensure consistency with existing voluntary safety programs, including the Aviation Safety Action Program, the Aviation Safety Reporting System, the Air Traffic Safety Action Plan, and flight operational quality assurance programs.\n#### 124. Safety culture and safety management review\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 30 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the inspector general of the Department of Transportation shall initiate an audit of the safety culture and the safety management system of the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn conducting the audit under subsection (a), the inspector general shall, at a minimum, evaluate\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe safety management system of the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization, including the functions and data sharing activities of such system at all air traffic control facilities;\n**(2)**\nwhether such system effectively coordinates safety assurance and safety risk management activities with external stakeholders consistent with FAA requirements for operators under section 5.57 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations;\n**(3)**\nwhich data analysis, safety assurance, and risk assessment processes failed to identify and mitigate the risk of potential midair collisions near Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport before January 29, 2025;\n**(4)**\nthe failure of the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization to recognize external compliance verification results as indicators of systemic traffic management, volume, and flow issues at Ronald Reagan Washington National Airport for which air traffic controllers were required to compensate to mitigate such issues;\n**(5)**\nthe failure of the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization to conduct annual reviews of helicopter route charts as required by FAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration ;\n**(6)**\nthe failure of the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization to understand and implement post-accident and post-incident drug and alcohol testing as required by Department of Transportation Order 3910.1D, titled Drug and Alcohol-Free Departmental Workplace Program ;\n**(7)**\nwhether there are fears of retaliation against persons identifying or reporting risks in accordance with the safety management system; and\n**(8)**\nhow the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization have addressed the findings and utilized the Safety Risk Management process in accordance with FAA Order 8040.4C, titled Safety Risk Management Policy (or any successor document) in the National Airspace System Helicopter Operations Helicopter Route Analysis of the FAA issued in April 2025.\n##### (c) Report of the inspector general\n**(1) In general**\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, the inspector general shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report on the audit conducted under subsection (a).\n**(2) Recommendations**\nThe inspector general shall include in the report submitted under paragraph (1)\u2014\n**(A)**\nrecommendations for actions the Secretary should take with respect to the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization to\u2014\n**(i)**\nstrengthen and adhere to the tenets of the safety management system;\n**(ii)**\nincrease transparency in the safety management system process, including by adopting policies that provide assurances to FAA employees that the Air Traffic Organization is addressing any identified safety issues;\n**(iii)**\nincrease data sharing and collaboration with external stakeholders;\n**(iv)**\nprotect against retaliation;\n**(v)**\nencourage open, nonpunitive communication; and\n**(vi)**\nfoster a just culture across the Air Traffic Organization and the Aviation Safety Management Organization;\n**(B)**\nrecommendations for actions the Secretary may take to ensure adequate oversight over the safety management system of the Air Traffic Organization; and\n**(C)**\nany other recommendations the inspector general determines appropriate.\n##### (d) Response to recommendations\nNot later than 120 days after submission of the report required under subsection (c)\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe Secretary shall respond to any recommendations in such report that are directed at the Department of Transportation or FAA, respectively; and\n**(2)**\nthe Secretary shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report describing how the Secretary intends to implement such recommendations.\n#### 125. Documentation of control position combinations\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 1 year after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall review and revise, as appropriate, procedures regarding the documentation of the combination of air traffic control position responsibilities, including each occurrence in which any air traffic control position is combined with any other position, including a local control position, operations supervisor, or controller-in-charge.\n##### (b) Requirements\nIn reviewing and revising the procedures described in subsection (a), the Administrator shall\u2014\n**(1)**\nevaluate procedures and guidance regarding the combination of controller position responsibilities described in subsection (a) that are in effect prior to the date of enactment of this Act;\n**(2)**\nexamine the feasibility of digitizing, or providing an electronic means of, the documentation described in subsection (a);\n**(3)**\nrequire the operations supervisor to periodically review documentation of occurrences of combined control position responsibilities described in subsection (a) and report on deviations from the standard operating procedures to the facility air traffic manager;\n**(4)**\nconsider air traffic facility type and staffing level; and\n**(5)**\nconsult with representatives of\u2014\n**(A)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(B)**\norganizations representing air traffic control managers and operational supervisors; and\n**(C)**\naviation safety experts with specific knowledge in information technology.\n##### (c) Briefing to Congress\nNot later than 1 year after the completion of the review required under subsection (a), the Administrator shall brief the appropriate committees of Congress on implementation of this section.\n##### (d) Rule of construction\nNothing in this section may be construed to interfere with any agreement between a governmental agency and the exclusive bargaining representative of air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code or section 7106(a) of title 5, United States Code.\n##### (e) Definitions\nIn this section:\n**(1) Controller-in-charge**\nThe term controller-in-charge means an air traffic control specialist performing duties of a shift supervisor in accordance with\u2014\n**(A)**\nFAA Order JO 7210.3EE, titled Facility Operation and Administration , issued on February 20, 2025; and\n**(B)**\nFAA Order JO 7110.65BB, titled Air Traffic Control , issued on February 20, 2025.\n**(2) Operations supervisor**\nThe term operations supervisor means managerial personnel responsible for the direct supervision of air traffic control operational personnel.\n#### 126. Review of miles-in-trail procedures or agreements\n##### (a) In general\nNot later than 60 days after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall complete a review of the miles-in-trail standards and procedures to determine if such standards provide for a separation of traffic that is appropriate for operational safety.\n##### (b) Considerations\nIn conducting the review under subsection (a), the Administrator may consider\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe accuracy of the criteria used to determine the miles-in-trail procedures for air traffic control facilities;\n**(2)**\nwhether additional criteria should be incorporated to more appropriately reflect the traffic volume and operational complexity of air traffic control facilities; and\n**(3)**\nthe findings and recommendations of the National Transportation Safety Board.\n##### (c) Standards update\nUpon completion of the review conducted under subsection (a), the Administrator shall update the miles-in-trail standards and procedures to ensure such standards and procedures are appropriate for operational safety.\n##### (d) Review of certain facilities\nNot later than 90 days after the completion of the review under subsection (a), the Administrator shall initiate a review of the miles-in-trail procedures or agreements at all air traffic control facilities located within Class B or Class C airspace to ensure such procedures or agreements provide for a separation of traffic that is appropriate for operational safety.\n##### (e) Consultation\nIn carrying out the review under subsection (d), the Administrator shall consult with, at minimum\u2014\n**(1)**\nthe exclusive bargaining representatives of the air traffic controllers certified under section 7111 of title 5, United States Code;\n**(2)**\norganizations representing air traffic control managers and operations supervisors;\n**(3)**\nsponsors and operators of airports with air traffic control facilities described in subsection (d);\n**(4)**\norganizations representing the certified collective bargaining representatives of pilots operating under part 121 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations; and\n**(5)**\nair carriers, business aviation, and general aviation operators with operations at airports with air traffic control facilities described in subsection (d).\n##### (f) Report\nNot later than 18 months after the date of enactment of this Act, the Administrator shall submit to the appropriate committees of Congress a report that includes\u2014\n**(1)**\na list of air traffic control facilities identified under subsection (d) as having miles-in-trail procedures or agreements that did not provide for a separation of aircraft traffic appropriate for operational safety; and\n**(2)**\nsteps that the Administrator has taken, or plans to take, to modify the miles-in-trail procedures or agreements at each facility listed under paragraph (1) to ensure such procedures or agreements provide for a separation of traffic that is appropriate for operational safety.\n#### 127. Closure of Helicopter Route 4\n##### (a) In general\nOperations on Helicopter Route 4, as such Route existed on January 29, 2025, on the segment located between Hains Point and the Woodrow Wilson Memorial Bridge in the District of Columbia shall be prohibited.\n##### (b) Segment elimination\nThe segment of Helicopter Route 4 described in subsection (a) shall remain eliminated from helicopter charts.\nII\nDepartment of Defense Matters\n#### 201. Department of Defense matters relating to aviation safety\nTitle 10, United States Code, is amended by inserting after chapter 157 the following new chapter:\n158 Aviation Safety Sec. 2655. Definitions. 2656. Memorandum of agreement. 2657. Required risk assessment and mitigation for special missions. 2658. Manned rotary wing aviation safety management system. 2659. Initial and recurring training on highly congested airspace. 2660. Flight data monitoring improvements. 2660a. Barometric altimeters. 2660b. Transponder maintenance. 2660c. Notifications and reports on certain near-miss events in National Capital Region. 2660d. Reports on individuals designated for purposes of special mission exclusion. 2660e. Rule of construction. 2655. Definitions In this chapter: (1) The term ADS\u2013B In means technology that receives and processes Automatic Dependent Surveillance\u2013Broadcast (ADS\u2013B) transmissions that are broadcast in accordance with parts 91.225 and 91.227 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations, and other aviation advisory information from ground stations, including Traffic Information Service\u2013Broadcast (TIS\u2013B) and Automatic Dependent Surveillance\u2013Rebroadcast (ADS\u2013R). (2) The term ADS\u2013B Out has the meaning given such term in part 91.227 of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations. (3) The term air traffic control services means services used for the monitoring, directing, control, and guidance of aircraft or flows of aircraft and for the safe conduct of flight, including communications, navigation, and surveillance services and the provision of aeronautical information. (4) The term appropriate congressional committees means the congressional defense committees, the Committee on Transportation and Infrastructure of the House of Representatives, and the Committee on Commerce, Science, and Transportation of the Senate. (5) The term Class B Mode C veil means any location described in part 91.225(d)(2) of title 14, Code of Federal Regulations. (6) The term collision prevention technology means technology that\u2014 (A) has ADS\u2013B In; (B) uses ADS\u2013B data; and (C) provides, and is configured to provide, alerting that is audible to the pilot and flight crew. (7) The term Department of Defense aircraft means any aircraft, either manned or unmanned, that is owned, operated, or controlled by the Department of Defense or operated pursuant to a contract entered into by the Department of Defense.
